  <raw>Honda Begins Fit EV Trials in China




Honda has started trial demonstrations of its Fit electric vehicle (EV) concepts in Guangzhou (China), according to a press release by the automaker. The tests are being carried out by the automaker in association with the government of the city of Guangzhou and Guangzhou Automobile Group. Guangqi Honda Automobile, Honda's automotive joint venture (JV) with Guangzhou Automobile Group, plans to begin local production of the EV in China before the end of 2012.

Significance:The trial is being conducted to determine the feasibility of alternative powertrains in the real-world urban transport environment and to identify technological issues to ensure the smooth deployment of alternative powertrains in the market. In addition, the trial's results will help in forming proposals for a charging infrastructure. The Fit, one of the most eagerly anticipated pure-electric vehicles from Honda, will make its debut next week at the Los Angeles Auto Show (seeUnited States: 26 October 2011:). The vehicle is remodelled from the popular five-seat gasoline (petrol)-engined Fit (known as the Jazz in select European and Asian markets). The subcompact hatchback is powered by a coaxial electric motor (also used in the Honda FCX Clarity hydrogen vehicle) and lithium-ion battery pack. The vehicle has a range of more than 150 kilometres based on the New European Driving Cycle (NEDC). The model also features a three-mode electric drive system, which allows the driver to select from Econ, Normal, and Sport modes. The electric car can be charged in less than six hours via a 220V power supply.</raw>
